  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer13435064846737387772">From the author of the bestselling "The Dangerous Book for Boys" <br/>He was born Temujin, the son of a khan, raised in a clan of hunters migrating across the rugged steppe.   <span id="freeText13435064846737387772" style="display:none">From the author of the bestselling "The Dangerous Book for Boys" <br />He was born Temujin, the son of a khan, raised in a clan of hunters migrating across the rugged steppe. Temujin's young life was shaped by a series of brutal acts: the betrayal of his father by a neighboring tribe and the abandonment of his entire family, cruelly left to die on the harsh plain. But Temujin endured--and from that moment on, he was driven by a singular fury: to survive in the face of death, to kill before being killed, and to conquer enemies who could come without warning from beyond the horizon. <br /> Through a series of courageous raids against the Tartars, Temujin's legend grew. And so did the challenges he faced--from the machinations of a Chinese ambassador to the brutal abduction of his young wife, Borte. Blessed with ferocious courage, it was the young warrior's ability to learn, to imagine, and to judge the hearts of others that propelled him to greater and greater power. Until Temujin was chasing a vision: to unite many tribes into one, to make the earth tremble under the hoofbeats of a thousand warhorses, to subject unknown nations and even empires to his will. "From the Hardcover edition."</span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/95596478-declan-ellis"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1554297835i/95596478._UY100_CR21,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/95596478-declan-ellis">Declan Ellis</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">For those of you interested in the answer to this question... <br/>I would agree with MA 15+ rating but add that the rape is not graphic. It is very strong<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">For those of you interested in the answer to this question... <br />I would agree with MA 15+ rating but add that the rape is not graphic. It is very strongly implied, but never explicitly shown. Besides, it is a significant event in Temujin's life which needed to be addressed, and therefore not in any way gratuitous. There is some pretty brutal violence, but again it is historically accurate and isn't too protracted. There is very little swearing and nothing that sexually explicit. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_2706110660" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2706110660" />
    <a title="Dana Ilie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21690081-dana-ilie"><img alt="Dana Ilie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584606424p2/21690081.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2706110660?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Ilie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Ilie" href="/user/show/21690081-dana-ilie">Dana Ilie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007201754" href="/book/show/1265656.Wolf_Of_The_Plains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21690081-dana-ilie?shelf=history">history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2706110660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6002142328198539821">The author writes in third person with the center of the narrative being the main character. The narrative's focus shifts to other characters' perspectives from time to time if their separate activities are significant in advancing the plot. The language is simple English with some actual Mongolian words used for commonplace objects to provide the necessary historical effect.<br/><br/>I loved this book! It is an extremely gripping narrative while providing the reader with an accurate picture of the histor</span>
  <span id="freeText6002142328198539821" style="display:none">The author writes in third person with the center of the narrative being the main character. The narrative's focus shifts to other characters' perspectives from time to time if their separate activities are significant in advancing the plot. The language is simple English with some actual Mongolian words used for commonplace objects to provide the necessary historical effect.<br /><br />I loved this book! It is an extremely gripping narrative while providing the reader with an accurate picture of the historical events of the time, thereby promoting learning while reading. It is very well researched. <br /><br />Wolf of the Plains is the first of the Conqueror series, devoted to the boyhood and youth of the future Genghis (or Temujin as he is known throughout this book). By the age of eleven Genghis’s father had been murdered and he was an outlaw on the Mongolian steppe. The gang of teenagers who gathered around him soon became expert killers, and the rest is history – or will be in the succeeding volumes.<br /><br />The story is vivid, fast and brutal, with a high body count. I do not know how much firsthand experience the author has of the Mongolian steppe, but it rings true. Now that Genghis has united the Mongols, we look forward to the conquest of the world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6002142328198539821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2303651605" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2303651605" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2303651605?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6568175-genghis">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">historical fiction fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2303651605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6708672371846268695"><b>Unbelievably good; this marked the first time I finished reading Iggulden’s work, and it’s VERY promising that this will become one of my favorite series.</b><br/><br/>Conn Iggulden isn’t exactly an unfamiliar name to me; despite the fact that he’s most well-known for his historical fiction works, Iggulden’s blurbs have been featured on some of my favorite fantasy books such as <i>The Faithful and the Fallen</i> series by John Gwynne and <i>The Realm of the Elderlings</i> series by Robin Hobb, to name a few. For years I’ve</span>
  <span id="freeText6708672371846268695" style="display:none"><b>Unbelievably good; this marked the first time I finished reading Iggulden’s work, and it’s VERY promising that this will become one of my favorite series.</b><br /><br />Conn Iggulden isn’t exactly an unfamiliar name to me; despite the fact that he’s most well-known for his historical fiction works, Iggulden’s blurbs have been featured on some of my favorite fantasy books such as <i>The Faithful and the Fallen</i> series by John Gwynne and <i>The Realm of the Elderlings</i> series by Robin Hobb, to name a few. For years I’ve been interested in reading his books, and from what I’ve gathered, his <i>Conqueror</i> series seems to be the most often regarded as his best works by his readers. And so here we are and my god, I seriously didn’t expect it to be this great.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “Mongolia is an unforgiving land. The boy, Temujin, was never cruel, and there is no record of him ever taking pleasure from the destruction of his enemies, but he was capable of utter ruthlessness.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><i>Genghis: Birth of an Empire</i>, alternatively called <i>Wolf of the Plains</i>, is the first installment in Conn Iggulden’s <i>Conqueror</i> series. This is a historical fiction series about Genghis Khan’s rise to power and if I’m not mistaken, eventually leading to his death and legacy. Genghis Khan, born Temujin, has been dead for almost a thousand years now, and yet his story and legends still live on. As much as I’d love to say that I know about Genghis Khan, I have to admit that my knowledge about him only goes as far as his terrifying ruthlessness and legacy of conquest; I didn’t know about his birth, background, and what led to his legends. <i>Birth of an Empire</i> depicts Temujin’s coming-of-age story; Iggulden expertly shows the contrast between his childhood and his legends. I found Iggulden’s decision to start Temujin’s story from the time he was still twelve years old to be an incredibly clever choice. It was super engrossing, shocking and, interesting to read Temujin’s growth and developments. What I found to be very intriguing was although it’s true that the sign of Temujin’s tendency for ruthlessness appeared since he was a child, it was the harsh events, lessons, and circumstances forced upon him that shaped and forged that trait towards its maximum potential. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “His childhood experiences created the man he would become, who would not bend or allow fear or weakness in any form. He cared nothing for possessions or wealth, only that his enemies fall.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />I truly think that Iggulden’s excelled as his characterizations of Temujin and his family in this book, especially for his brothers and parents; they are all so well-fleshed out characters with a personality that’s distinctive from each other. As I’ve mentioned before, Temujin’s natural instinct lies in his strength, charisma, and ruthlessness; he’s simply a natural-born leader following the footsteps of his father: Yesugei. Then there’s Kashar and Kachiun the loyal one, Temuge the fearful, Bekter the devious, and Hoelun the strong mother who protects them all as best as she could. With such well-realized characters, Iggulden tells a story revolving around the theme of survival of the fittest superbly. Mongolia was an unforgiving land, both in deadly tribal rivalries and nature. Reading Temujin and his family trying their utmost best to survive was compelling; it’s unimaginable for me to put myself in their position. Seriously, they were dealing with extreme starvation in weather that’s extremely cold (-20 up to -40 degree Celcius.) Death walks with them every step of their way, and it nurtured their courage, strength, and camaraderie; they became the death bringer instead of letting the weight of injustice bringing them down. I loved reading about all of these; there’s something immensely inspiring in the physical and mental prowess they unleashed to deal with the harsh realities of their world.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Courage cannot be left like bones in a bag. It must be brought out and shown the light again and again, growing stronger each time. If you think it will keep for the times you need it, you are wrong. It is like any other part of your strength. If you ignore it, the bag will be empty when you need it most.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />One important thing to note, and surprising to me, is that Iggulden utilized a head-hopping narrative to tell the multi-perspective narration. For those of you who don’t know, I hated this kind of storytelling style; I tend to find head-hopping confusing and distracting. However, Iggulden was tremendously skillful in implementing this narrative; I never felt lost and I was able to easily follow which character’s head I’m in. Not only the flow of the prose never disrupted by the head-hopping narrative, but I also found myself completely engrossed by every POV switch; it was entertaining to see Iggulden juggles the variety of characters perspectives and emotions in scenes that are full of tension and drama. Do remember, this almost never worked for me, the only other books where I found this style working for me was for Dune by Frank Herbert and Paternus by Dyrk Ashton, and if I may be honest, none of them did it as well as Iggulden in this book and hopefully series.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “There was no bond stronger than that between those who have risked their lives in each other’s company.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Reread excluded, <i>Genghis: Birth of an Empire</i> ended up becoming my first full 5-stars rating in two months. Conqueror is often hailed as Iggulden’s best work, and although I’ve read only the first book, I can certainly understand why this has become a common consensus. <i>Genghis: Birth of an Empire</i> is a stunning piece of historical fiction that tells a gripping story about survival and a legendary figure’s rise to power. This book was about Temujin’s coming-of-age and his struggle in uniting Mongol; it seems like the next installment, <i>Genghis: Lords of the Bow</i>, will start telling Genghis’s spreading conquest as one of the most terrifying rulers of our history, and you bet I will be jumping into it immediately.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“He had a vision of a nation. The incredible martial skills of the Mongol tribes had always been wasted against each other. From nothing, surrounded by enemies, Temujin rose to unite them all. What came next would shake the world.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780385344210/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br /><br /><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/11/07/book-review-genghis-birth-of-an-empire-conqueror-1-by-conn-iggulden/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6708672371846268695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_793476731" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793476731" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/793476731?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007353255" href="/book/show/9694318-wolf-of-the-plains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793476731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2880040924521623719"><i>"He holds blood in his right hand," she whispered. "He will walk with death all his life."</i><br/><br/>Spread out across the steppes, the Mongols are a divided people. Infighting and enmity have turned them into a scattered collection of tribes barely scraping by. Until there comes a man destined to lead them all to boundless glory and conquest. The second son of Yesugei, chieftain of the Wolves. A boy called Temujin, who would later pass into legend as the greatest conqueror in all history.<br/><br/>Leave it to Conn </span>
  <span id="freeText2880040924521623719" style="display:none"><i>"He holds blood in his right hand," she whispered. "He will walk with death all his life."</i><br><br>Spread out across the steppes, the Mongols are a divided people. Infighting and enmity have turned them into a scattered collection of tribes barely scraping by. Until there comes a man destined to lead them all to boundless glory and conquest. The second son of Yesugei, chieftain of the Wolves. A boy called Temujin, who would later pass into legend as the greatest conqueror in all history.<br><br>Leave it to Conn Iggulden to tell the tale of a legendary historical figure in the most captivating and spectacular fashion…<br><br>The story of the barbarian warlord who would later be known as Genghis Khan is a deeply fascinating one. It’s the tale of a man who went from being a chieftain’s son in a minor tribe to ruling the greatest empire the world had ever seen at the time. The first part of that tale is retold by Conn Iggulden in this book, and it’s an amazing journey to be brought along on.<br><br>I was actually a bit worried early on as the book wasn’t particularly impressive until almost halfway through. The early parts were quite slow and contained little to no suspense at all. However, once the plot actually got going, there was no turning back.<br><br>There were times when I thought this book was the best I’d read this year for sure. Unfortunately it failed to reach that level in the end, but it got pretty close. Iggulden is often accused of completely ignoring historical accuracy, and often that’s even true, but what does it matter when you can tell stories like this? In just about every single aspect of writing, he’s second only to Bernard Cornwell himself in this particular genre.<br><br>As the opening book of a series, this was really good. It sets the stage for what is to come, with an interesting setting and set of characters. For some reason it seemed a little bit too simple, in that the storyline, the number of important characters and the area in which the story takes place are all really limited; but then again, this is only the first book, and it serves its purpose as an introduction and a taste of what is to come. So far, I must say that the series is not quite as good as Iggulden’s <i>Emperor</i> series, but it definitely has the potential for it.<br><br>The best part about the whole thing was that I was dragged by the heels out of my terrible reading funk. It didn’t even take the whole book to do it, just this particular quote, which might just be the best historical fiction line I’ve encountered…<br><br><b>
  <i>“I am the land, and the bones of the hills," he said fiercely, "I am the winter. When I am dead, I will come for you all in the coldest nights.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437489188i/15589249._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2880040924521623719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81820989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81820989" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81820989?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=christmas-gift">christmas-gift</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81820989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4754387283108157754">Temujin, the son of Yesugei, khan of the Wolves, goes to a neighboring tribe to find a wife. While he's away, his father is murdered by a gang of Tartars. Worse still, his father's friend usurps the role of khan and leaves Temujin and his family to die on the steppe. Can Temujin and his family survive long enough to get revenge on the Tartars and regain control of the Wolves?<br/><br/>The story of Temujin and his rise to uniting the tribes against the Tartars is a powerful one. Temujin goes through a lot </span>
  <span id="freeText4754387283108157754" style="display:none">Temujin, the son of Yesugei, khan of the Wolves, goes to a neighboring tribe to find a wife. While he's away, his father is murdered by a gang of Tartars. Worse still, his father's friend usurps the role of khan and leaves Temujin and his family to die on the steppe. Can Temujin and his family survive long enough to get revenge on the Tartars and regain control of the Wolves?<br /><br />The story of Temujin and his rise to uniting the tribes against the Tartars is a powerful one. Temujin goes through a lot of hell from the age of twelve onward, from being abandoned on the steppe during winter, to being imprisoned in a pit and being urinated on, to having his wife kidnapped and raped by Tartars. Once he started uniting the tribes, even I felt like riding with the young khan. While he's not always likeable, he's definitely a charismatic character.<br /><br />The action scenes were by far the highlight of the book. People get peppered with arrows or hacked to death by swords on a fairly regular basis. While Iggulden plays fast and loose with history, it's still a great story. And since I'm already aware I'm reading fiction, I don't really care about historical accuracy. Iggulden's writing makes for an engaging read. You will not easily be able to put this down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4754387283108157754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2322673925" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2322673925" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63168028-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516912354p2/63168028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2322673925?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/63168028-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007201754" href="/book/show/1265656.Wolf_Of_The_Plains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2322673925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15430219156800395374"><b>Visionary</b><br/><i>Wolf of the Plains</i> is a fictional adaptation of one of the World's greatest leaders. A leader that built one of the greatest empires ever seen, if not the greatest. In this first book of the <i>Conqueror</i> series, we see Temujin from his childhood, cast out of his father's Wolf tribe, to uniting a warrior race that would conquer many lands and be named the first Great Khan of the Plains.<br/><br/>Yesugei, the khan of the Wolf tribe, his wife, Hoelun, his sons Temujin, Bekter, Khasar, Kachiun and Temug</span>
  <span id="freeText15430219156800395374" style="display:none"><b>Visionary</b><br /><i>Wolf of the Plains</i> is a fictional adaptation of one of the World's greatest leaders. A leader that built one of the greatest empires ever seen, if not the greatest. In this first book of the <i>Conqueror</i> series, we see Temujin from his childhood, cast out of his father's Wolf tribe, to uniting a warrior race that would conquer many lands and be named the first Great Khan of the Plains.<br /><br />Yesugei, the khan of the Wolf tribe, his wife, Hoelun, his sons Temujin, Bekter, Khasar, Kachiun and Temuge, and his daughter Borte, live a warring and perfidious existence against other tribes on the Mongolian steppes. Yesugei dies after an attack and leaves the leadership open to Eeluk (his bondsman) with his sons not being old enough to take control. Eeluk exiles Hoelun and her children to live an abandoned harsh life with no dwelling, no food, no animals, no horses and no weapons. Surely as winter descends it is only a matter of time before they all perish. <br /><br />And so begins the engrossing story of how Temujin transitions himself into Genghis Khan's and assumes leadership of a disparate people. It was amazing how aware Temujin was of his surroundings and people and how he used strategy, tactics, politics, force and cunning to firstly survive and then unite the Mongol tribes. The greatest battle in his early life was against the Tartars, which his father’s clan, the Wolves, come to participate. After the victory, Temujin and Eeluk fight to resolve old vendettas, leaving Temujin victorious and leader of many of the tribes on the plains.<br /><br />The book is a wonderful example of historical fiction where we get to know so much about the times of the foundation and growth of the Mongol empire and the birth of Genghis Khan. The narration creates a vivid and compelling insight into the characters that are inspirational, loyal and battle-hard, with a storyline that is breath-taking. The harshness of the environment and how they survived is exceptionally well portrayed. <blockquote>
  <i>"We are the Silver people, the Mongols. When they ask tell them there are no tribes. Tell them I am khan of the sea of grass, and they will know me by my name, as Genghis."</i>
</blockquote> Many people's will come to know him and the fact that his story is still held as one of the greatest leadership and military examples in history is a testament to his achievements. What is probably more impressive is that he had a very clever strategy of building and maintaining an empire that would survive - and for long enough it did.<br /><br />I loved this book and with Conn Iggulden's imaginary I felt it come to life. I would highly recommend this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15430219156800395374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1407291399" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1407291399" />
    <a title="Lizzy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30575403-lizzy"><img alt="Lizzy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512052362p2/30575403.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1407291399?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lizzy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lizzy" href="/user/show/30575403-lizzy">Lizzy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30575403-lizzy?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30575403-lizzy?shelf=stars-4">stars-4</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30575403-lizzy?shelf=read-years-ago">read-years-ago</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1407291399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2204261773247086575">I've always been curious about almost anything that happened in the past. As far away as high school and college I thoroughly enjoyed history. And in the recent years, I rediscovered this love of mine. When I saw these historical novels about Genghis Khan I could not resist. <br/><br/>After uniting the Mongol tribes <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1279686.Genghis_Birth_of_an_Empire__Conqueror___1_' title='Genghis Birth of an Empire (Conqueror, #1) by Conn Iggulden' rel='nofollow noopener'> Genghis: Birth of an Empire</a>, Genghis later on targets and conquers the Chin <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1632833.Genghis_Lords_of_the_Bow__Conqueror___2_' title='Genghis Lords of the Bow (Conqueror, #2) by Conn Iggulden' rel='nofollow noopener'> Genghis: Lords of the Bow</a>. I fully enjoyed the two books. Despite the difficulty of telling fiction from fact, it </span>
  <span id="freeText2204261773247086575" style="display:none">I've always been curious about almost anything that happened in the past. As far away as high school and college I thoroughly enjoyed history. And in the recent years, I rediscovered this love of mine. When I saw these historical novels about Genghis Khan I could not resist. <br /><br />After uniting the Mongol tribes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1279686.Genghis_Birth_of_an_Empire__Conqueror___1_" title="Genghis Birth of an Empire (Conqueror, #1) by Conn Iggulden" rel="nofollow noopener"> Genghis: Birth of an Empire</a>, Genghis later on targets and conquers the Chin <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1632833.Genghis_Lords_of_the_Bow__Conqueror___2_" title="Genghis Lords of the Bow (Conqueror, #2) by Conn Iggulden" rel="nofollow noopener"> Genghis: Lords of the Bow</a>. I fully enjoyed the two books. Despite the difficulty of telling fiction from fact, it was still worthwhile. However, this is not a history book, and there's plenty of room for creativity. <br /><br />The book certainly has plenty of endless battles and plenty and discusses war strategies. The most famous and gruesome battle, described in detail by Iggulden, is the one fought at the Badger Mouth. To combat the Mongol advance, the Chin had assembled approximately half a million soldiers (versus the Mongol's 100 thousand) and stationed them at Badger Mouth. However, the Chin appeared to have been overly confident in their numbers and mainly in their defensive position: Genghis eventually circumvented their defenses by sending part of his men over the peaks surrounding the pass, something the Chin thought impossible, allowing him to encircle the much larger army. As a result, he slaughtered thousands and the enemy’s soldiers and practically destroyed its army. <br /><br />Advancing, the Mongols came to besiege the Chin capital of Yenking (modern day Beijing). There Genghis faced the hard fact of an army (with memories of their own inner resentments) that he had to keep not only fed with spirits but with battles and triumphs. After a siege of years, the city finally surrendered. Regardless, it shows a ruthless man that must have been brilliant and astute to have conquered so much, considering he came from a nomadic and small tribe and his crudeness. <br /><br />I enjoyed reading Iggulden’s version of life in the China of that time, how the Mongol and Chinese mixed and related to each to each other. Moreover, reading this book started me into a new interest in reading military fiction that extends into today.<br /><br />I loved both volumes, although I have yet to read the third. I recommend Iggulden's Genghis Khan story to fans of non-romantic historical and military fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2204261773247086575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_520230346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/520230346" />
    <a title="Tim The Enchanter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5654692-tim-the-enchanter"><img alt="Tim The Enchanter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386188040p2/5654692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/520230346?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim The Enchanter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim The Enchanter" href="/user/show/5654692-tim-the-enchanter">Tim The Enchanter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6568175-genghis">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=my-ebooks">my-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=favorite-books-of-2014">favorite-books-of-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=2014-top-10">2014-top-10</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer520230346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5730636465869042053"><b>
  <a href='http://theliterarylawyer.ca/2015-gavel-awards/' rel='nofollow noopener'> My #10 Read of 2014 </a>
</b><br/><br/><b> <u> Perfectly Executed Historical Fiction - 5 Stars </u> </b><br/><br/>Action, Drama, Romance, History and Suspense, Birth of an Empire has it all. This volume robbed me of several full nights of sleep and I need to press on to see how the story would resolve. The story unfolds quickly while at the same time the author maintains his eye for detail. Birth of an Empire is my favorite type of HF. If you enjoy HF that places a premium on action and military (or in this case raiders) and war, th</span>
  <span id="freeText5730636465869042053" style="display:none"><b>
  <a href="http://theliterarylawyer.ca/2015-gavel-awards/" rel="nofollow noopener"> My #10 Read of 2014 </a>
</b><br /><br /><b> <u> Perfectly Executed Historical Fiction - 5 Stars </u> </b><br /><br />Action, Drama, Romance, History and Suspense, Birth of an Empire has it all. This volume robbed me of several full nights of sleep and I need to press on to see how the story would resolve. The story unfolds quickly while at the same time the author maintains his eye for detail. Birth of an Empire is my favorite type of HF. If you enjoy HF that places a premium on action and military (or in this case raiders) and war, then you will enjoy this novel.<br /><br /><u> Plot summary </u><br /><br />The story tells of the early years of Temujin, or Genghis Khan as most people would know him. We begin in the Pre-Teen years of Genghis and we learn how his relationship with his father and his brother, molded him into the man he would become. The novel covers much the sparsely documented childhood experience from his family's banishment, to his imprisonment and on toward his ultimate quest for victory.<br /><br /><u> The Good </u><br /><br /><b> They Did What? </b><br /><br />The Author did a wonderful job of infusing the story with the practices, beliefs, prejudices and realities of the of the Mongol people during this period of history. From the warriors ability to live on mares milk and blood for extended periods, their social structure, their weapons and their customs, you are transported to the Mongolian plains and your home becomes a Mongolian ger while you enjoy the story. The Author not only consulted the ancient texts regarding Genghis Khan, but he spent time amongst the Mongolian people before writing the books. His effort and dedication was obvious.<br /><br /><b> Genghis is my Friend </b><br /><br />Like any other genre, HF has its own pitfalls to avoid. One such pitfall is focus on the period of time to the detriment of the characters. In this story, the author present a well balanced story. As stated above, the reader is firmly grounded in the place and time while at same time, the characters are bold, vibrant and multi-dimensional. The reader is presented with a vivid picture of not only Genghis but his four brothers, his parents (especially his father), his wife and his major enemies. This results in a well rounded story that allow for full immersion.<br /><br /><u> The Bad </u><br /><br /><b> Take it Easy, I'm so Tired </b><br /><br />As is most 5 stars review, I have little criticism for the book. Firstly, the story robbed me of many hours of sleep. On more than one night, when my bedside clock was reading 1 am, I forced myself to shut the kindle and close my eyes. Outside of this, the only minor complaint is the description of the battle and fights. The pace of the book is quick and little space is wasted. Unfortunately, this results in some rather quick descriptions of battle and important events. In this case, it did not affect my rating as the battles were a minor part of the book.<br /><br /><b> Final Thoughts </b><br /><br />In my opinion, this is a perfect specimen of HF. I enjoyed it and it is easily the best book I have read this year and I anticipate it will make my top 10 at the end of the year. Overall, the story is compelling. While the average reader will have some idea of the sheer force that Genghis Kahn ultimately became, that knowledge is far more amazing when you consider his humble beginnings. A must read.<br /><br /><u> Audiobook Notes </u><br /><br /><b> <u> Content Advisories </u> </b><br /><br />It is difficult to find commentary on the sex/violence/language content of book if you are interested. I make an effort to give you the information so you can make an informed decision before reading. *Disclaimer* I do not take note or count the occurrences of adult language as I read. I am simply giving approximations.<br /><br />Scale 1 - Lowest 5 - Highest<br /><br /><u> Sex </u> - <b> 2.5 </b><br /><br />There is a small amount of sex in the book. There are several instances where sex between the characters is implied. Beyond consensual sex, there were several instances of rape. Most of the instances were comments that rape had occurred or would occur but there was one scene in which there was an attempted rape. While it was not graphic, there was some mild description of previous instances. One of the characters states his wish to use the service of a prostitute on several occasions. Overall, the sexual content served as context for the time and was not graphic.<br /><br /><u> Language </u> - <b> 2 </b><br /><br />The language in the book was the traditional adult language. The derogatory terms were specific to the time. While the characters would often refer to others with these terms, they would not be considered swearing by todays standards.<br /><br /><u> Violence </u> - <b> 4 </b><br /><br />The story was told in a violent time. Fight and battles between tribes was constant. From the early stages there are multiple murders that are moderately graphic. A character is subjected to abuse and forms of torture. This is moderately graphic. As Genghis ages, the violence increases. There is a particularly graphic scene in which part of person heart is eaten. Violence is a persistent theme in the story. While it is plentiful, the moderate graphic nature of the majority leads to a 4 rating. You may wish to skip this novel if you are sensitive to violence and death.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5730636465869042053" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9559740970914728995">(In UK, this book is entitled <a href='http://www.amazon.co.uk/Wolf-Plains-Conqueror-Conn-Iggulden/dp/0007201753/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&s=books&qid=1255073985&sr=8-1' rel='nofollow noopener'>"Wolf of the Plains"</a>)<br/>A more harsh childhood is hard to imagine! <br/><br/>Although this book gallops along at Conn Iggulden's usual pace, I was continually tempted to leap ahead to find out what happened next. That makes it much more of a chapter-turner than merely a page-turner, and the narrative left me quite breathless at times!<br/><br/>Temujin is the son of the khan of one of the many Mongol tribes who are in continual, violent conflict. Without spoiling the story for you, his cir</span>
  <span id="freeText9559740970914728995" style="display:none">(In UK, this book is entitled <a href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/Wolf-Plains-Conqueror-Conn-Iggulden/dp/0007201753/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;s=books&amp;qid=1255073985&amp;sr=8-1" rel="nofollow noopener">"Wolf of the Plains"</a>)<br />A more harsh childhood is hard to imagine! <br /><br />Although this book gallops along at Conn Iggulden's usual pace, I was continually tempted to leap ahead to find out what happened next. That makes it much more of a chapter-turner than merely a page-turner, and the narrative left me quite breathless at times!<br /><br />Temujin is the son of the khan of one of the many Mongol tribes who are in continual, violent conflict. Without spoiling the story for you, his circumstances force him to grow up very quickly rather than lose his life. As the story unfolds, Temujin faces death many times and learns from his terrifying experiences. His list of those on whom he determines to wreak revenge grows as you read. Eventually, he becomes the respected, feared and uncompromising leader of the great horde which dominated two continents during that age.<br /><br />Had his childhood been easy, he would probably have settled down with a couple of wives and a few goats. Historic record shows otherwise, but that record hardly brings Ghengis Khan's tale to life in the way that Iggulden has managed in this book.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to anybody, and would challenge them to resist being swept along by such a brilliantly told story. I just can't wait to get my hands on the next episode, "Lords of the Bow," in January 2008.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2906292608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6899068356368755862"><i>"I am the land, the bones of the hills," he said fiercely, "I am the winter. When I am dead, I will come for you all in the coldest nights."</i><br/><br/><b>Brilliant!</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/119121.Conn_Iggulden' title='Conn Iggulden' rel='nofollow noopener'>Conn Iggulden</a>`s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1279686.Genghis_Birth_of_an_Empire__Conqueror___1_' title='Genghis Birth of an Empire (Conqueror, #1) by Conn Iggulden' rel='nofollow noopener'>Genghis: Birth of an Empire</a> is an incredible read. There are so many high moments in this book, that you will not be able to keep the book down until it's completed. <br/><br/>The book is so well written and every situation is so vividly described, that I actually felt myself being there, when the Great Khan was born to growing up to become G</span>
  <span id="freeText6899068356368755862" style="display:none"><i>"I am the land, the bones of the hills," he said fiercely, "I am the winter. When I am dead, I will come for you all in the coldest nights."</i><br /><br /><b>Brilliant!</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/119121.Conn_Iggulden" title="Conn Iggulden" rel="nofollow noopener">Conn Iggulden</a>`s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1279686.Genghis_Birth_of_an_Empire__Conqueror___1_" title="Genghis Birth of an Empire (Conqueror, #1) by Conn Iggulden" rel="nofollow noopener">Genghis: Birth of an Empire</a> is an incredible read. There are so many high moments in this book, that you will not be able to keep the book down until it's completed. <br /><br />The book is so well written and every situation is so vividly described, that I actually felt myself being there, when the Great Khan was born to growing up to become Genghis Khan. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/119121.Conn_Iggulden" title="Conn Iggulden" rel="nofollow noopener">Conn Iggulden</a> has done such an amazing job of bringing to life the realities, habits, beliefs, attitudes, culture and practices of Mongolian tribes and families. Clearly, Conn has done so much research and hard work on this book. In the introduction, he mentions about having stayed in Mongolia, to learn and understand. <br /><br />At any point, you will not feel slowing down or resting. The Great Khan is so focused and clear, right from his birth. There is no time to waste, as much needs to be accomplished (read as to be conquered).<br /><br /><i>"There is no bond stronger than that between those who have risked their lives in each other's company."</i></span>

<div id="review_954446450" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/954446450" />
    <a title="Conor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30552336-conor"><img alt="Conor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400278909p2/30552336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/954446450?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Conor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Conor" href="/user/show/30552336-conor">Conor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer954446450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3154611038967976101">2.5 Stars<br/><br/>This was a decent work of historical fiction with a brilliantly realised setting that was ultimately let down by some pacing and characterisation issues. <br/><br/>I should probably say at this point that I'm a massive history nerd and I've read a lot about Genghis Khan. Some of my complaints about this book (and probably part of the reason I'm rating it lower than most of my friends) are down to the way that some events and characters were presented by Iggulden in contrast with my previous under</span>
  <span id="freeText3154611038967976101" style="display:none">2.5 Stars<br /><br />This was a decent work of historical fiction with a brilliantly realised setting that was ultimately let down by some pacing and characterisation issues. <br /><br />I should probably say at this point that I'm a massive history nerd and I've read a lot about Genghis Khan. Some of my complaints about this book (and probably part of the reason I'm rating it lower than most of my friends) are down to the way that some events and characters were presented by Iggulden in contrast with my previous understanding of what happened. I can't say whose interpretation is better... although if the measurement is sales of historical fiction books probably Iggulden. <br /><br />Genghis Khan's rise to power is one of the most incredible stories ever told. It's a story of betrayal, hardship, violence, ambition and revenge. While a lot of these aspects were carried over into this book, I was still a bit disappointed with the pace of the story, especially early on. For the first half of this book Temujin suffers betrayal and scorn at every turn. Despite often vowing revenge he doesn't achieve anything before running into the next conflict. All of these conflicts building up, with no resolution in sight, made it really difficult foe me to enjoy these parts of the book. <br /><br />For me the strongest element of this book was the setting. Iggulden does an incredible job of bringing the harshness and brutality of the Mongolian plains to life. The vivid description of the landscape made the accounts of Genghis' family struggling to survive on the barren plains an especially gripping and intense section. The determination of Mongolian warriors is also explored as we see these men fire bows (with a draw weight of 200 pounds, all held on a couple of fingers) from horseback and survive days of strenuous riding and fighting on milk and blood from their mares. Mongol society as a whole is also written with a great eye for detail. Throughout the book 'Gers', 'deals' and other important features of the Mongolian lifestyle were drilled into my brain. <br /><br />Throughout this story there are a number of interesting characters but I was disappointed by their lack of depth and complexity. Genghis' brothers play major roles, both as part of the story and as part of the Khan's ambitions. The brothers were some of my favourite characters and their relationships with each other were especially well-written. Hoelun, Genghis' formidable mother, was a character I was really psyched to read about. For the most part I really enjoyed her parts but (Spoilers*) I was frustrated by the drama between her and Gengis after he killed Bekter. Her blindness to Bekters selfishness and brutality and the fact that she seemingly didn't mind that he was feeding himself while allowing the rest of the family to starve was completely at odds with her usual pragmatism. Historical fact incoming: Bekter wasn't even her son. He was actually her husband's son from a previous marriage so it wouldn't really make sense for her to be upset that her son had removed a rival to himself and threat to the family. <br /><br />I was also disappointed by the Genghis-Borte romance as I've always considered their relationship to be an incredible narrative. The story of how the most ruthlessly effective conqueror to ever live went to war for the first time to save the woman he loved was really moving. I was disappointed with the lack of depth and passion in their relationship in this book. Okay that was a pretty wussy point so to balance it out: That scene where Genghis and his brothers killed those herders was awesome. Killing and looting = man stuff. <br /><br />While the descriptions of fighting were suitably gritty and brutal I was disappointed at the lack of exploration of Genghis' military strategy. At one point Genghis' forces win a battle despite being outnumbered (possibly badly outnumbered) by simply charging straight at the enemy. Later on Genghis takes control of 3 of the most powerful tribes in Mongolia by murdering a Khan and fighting a couple of duels. I was hoping to get an insight into the long years of constant war and alliance making that turned Temujin into 'Genghis Khan' but instead a well-timed invasion from the evil Tartars forces everyone to agree to join up with Genghis. <br /><br />Overall this was a decent piece of historical fiction with a lot of good qualities. I might check out the continuation of this story sometime to see if I can better get into the continuation of the story of Genghis Khan.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3154611038967976101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1380343939?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alice Poon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alice Poon" href="/user/show/28700577-alice-poon">Alice Poon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385339513" href="/book/show/330945.Genghis">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28700577-alice-poon?shelf=asia-themed">asia-themed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28700577-alice-poon?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1380343939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4282288303930140807"><br/>I started reading this novel with a strange curiosity about the early life of Genghis Khan, having already read three non-fiction titles about his life-time conquests and those of his offspring. I ended up being deeply touched by the skilful crafting of a poignant coming-of-age tale portraying the young and fearless tribal leader. His unbeatable will to survive as a precocious male child of an ostracized and fatherless family in the harshest of environments is destined to make him a formidable t</span>
  <span id="freeText4282288303930140807" style="display:none"><br />I started reading this novel with a strange curiosity about the early life of Genghis Khan, having already read three non-fiction titles about his life-time conquests and those of his offspring. I ended up being deeply touched by the skilful crafting of a poignant coming-of-age tale portraying the young and fearless tribal leader. His unbeatable will to survive as a precocious male child of an ostracized and fatherless family in the harshest of environments is destined to make him a formidable tribal head and chart the winning course of his inimitable adult life. Still a young teen, he had to face the sudden loss of a father, heartless betrayals, constant cold and hunger, homelessness, deadly traps and all kinds of brutal life threats. It is hard not to believe that there is some truth in fiction in this case, as it can probably be surmised that what happens to a person in his/her early formative years is most likely to give shape to his/her character.<br /><br />The novel is sprinkled with occasional gory scenes and graphic details, but also does not lack sentimental episodes. Overall, it is a gripping read.<br /><br />The author explains in a note that his chief source of historical details largely comes from Arthur Waley’s translation of a Chinese version of “The Secret History of the Mongols”, the original Mongolian text of which was written in the 13th century, after the death of Genghis Khan.<br /><br />Late last year I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/679544.The_History_And_The_Life_Of_Chinggis_Khan_The_Secret_History_Of_The_Mongols" title="The History And The Life Of Chinggis Khan The Secret History Of The Mongols by Urgunge Onon" rel="nofollow noopener">The History And The Life Of Chinggis Khan: The Secret History Of The Mongols</a>, which is the Mongolian scholar Urgunge Onon’s translation of the original 13th century text, and early this year I read Jack Weatherford’s two non-fiction titles: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/93426.Genghis_Khan_and_the_Making_of_the_Modern_World" title="Genghis Khan and the Making of the Modern World by Jack Weatherford" rel="nofollow noopener">Genghis Khan and the Making of the Modern World</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6648001.The_Secret_History_of_the_Mongol_Queens_How_the_Daughters_of_Genghis_Khan_Rescued_His_Empire" title="The Secret History of the Mongol Queens How the Daughters of Genghis Khan Rescued His Empire by Jack Weatherford" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History of the Mongol Queens: How the Daughters of Genghis Khan Rescued His Empire</a>. These three books together gave me a pretty good picture of the times and lives of Genghis Khan and his successors.<br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4282288303930140807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8306467352440969289">3.5 to 4.0 stars. Genghis Khan is a historical figure that has always fascinated me because of how little is known about him despite having once ruled much of the known world. This story does an excellent job of telling a compelling story while staying, for the most part, true to the historical record (the author explains in an afterward certain "creative licenses" taken for narratrive purposes). I really liked the sense of place established by the narrative as well as the extremely harsh condit</span>
  <span id="freeText8306467352440969289" style="display:none">3.5 to 4.0 stars. Genghis Khan is a historical figure that has always fascinated me because of how little is known about him despite having once ruled much of the known world. This story does an excellent job of telling a compelling story while staying, for the most part, true to the historical record (the author explains in an afterward certain "creative licenses" taken for narratrive purposes). I really liked the sense of place established by the narrative as well as the extremely harsh conditions under which Genghis lived. <br /><br />This first volume of what I believe to be a trilogy tells the story of Temujin (birth name of Genghis) from his early years to the beginning of his rise to power. As good as this story was, I am confident that the next book will be even better given that it will deal with Temujin's conquest of much of Asia which should make for fascinating reading. <br /><br />Strongly recommended for fans of historical fiction. One final note: I listened to the audiobook narrated by Stefan Rudnicki who did his usual AMAZING job with the story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8306467352440969289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3578868855" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3578868855" />
    <a title="Debbie Zapata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22110057-debbie-zapata"><img alt="Debbie Zapata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451631863p2/22110057.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3578868855?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie Zapata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie Zapata" href="/user/show/22110057-debbie-zapata">Debbie Zapata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385339513" href="/book/show/330945.Genghis">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22110057-debbie-zapata?shelf=2020printbooks">2020printbooks</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3578868855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer127614339830186033">Oct 5, 11pm ~~ Review tomorrow.<br/><br/>Oct 7, 1pm ~~ Not quite 'tomorrow' but here is my review. lol<br/><br/>This is the second time I have read this first of the author's five volume series about Genghis Khan. I remember reading book two many years pre-GR, and when I realized it was part of a series I found this title at my local library. But I never read any of the others, since they were all published during the years I was living in Mexico. <br/><br/>Recently, thanks to The HU band, I have reignited my interest in Mon</span>
  <span id="freeText127614339830186033" style="display:none">Oct 5, 11pm ~~ Review tomorrow.<br /><br />Oct 7, 1pm ~~ Not quite 'tomorrow' but here is my review. lol<br /><br />This is the second time I have read this first of the author's five volume series about Genghis Khan. I remember reading book two many years pre-GR, and when I realized it was part of a series I found this title at my local library. But I never read any of the others, since they were all published during the years I was living in Mexico. <br /><br />Recently, thanks to The HU band, I have reignited my interest in Mongolia and have been reading a few non-fiction works about the country. Then I saw a GR friend's rating of one of the books in this series and I realized now was the perfect time to collect and read them myself. <br /><br />So here we are. Now even though I had read this book before, I only clearly remembered the first couple of chapters, in which Temujin and his brothers climb a cliff to try and capture a young eagle to give to their father. There is of course a great rivalry between the boys. They all want to be the one who actually captures one of the prized birds and earn glory in their father's eyes. Who will be the one to claim that glory?<br /><br />After that I didn't remember details so it was like reading the book for the first time. Of course we all know how it turns out, since Genghis Khan was such a force of history, but this telling of his early years, from birth to the point he becomes that force, is fascinating and hypnotic, very hard to put down. <br /><br />At the end, the author provides a few details in which he gives his main sources, and explains that certain events later in the book were time-compressed from a few months to a few days. This explains some of the doubts Genghis could never overcome in actual life about his first born son.<br /><br />As I read about the way this man brought the various groups together into one nation, I couldn't help but wonder how different the histories of other countries might have been if they had experienced such a person in their early days. Take Mexico, for example. There were and still are dozens of groups of indigenous people throughout the country. The Aztecs were merely the strongest at the time the Spaniards arrived, they were not necessarily the leaders of of a unified people in the way Genghis and his family became in Mongolia. The people in Mexico were never united, they were conquered from within and without before they ever had a sense of Nation. A person cannot help but wonder what might have been, not just in Mexico but in any country that suffered through conquest and domination. <br /><br />I have already started with the second book, and will be working my way through the series over the next couple of weeks. And I have added The Secret History Of The Mongols to my wish list at my favorite online used bookseller. I think it would be awesome to read this story from its source! <br /><br /> <br /><br /> <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="127614339830186033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_311688200" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311688200" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1019174-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555890512p2/1019174.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311688200?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/1019174-terence">Terence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385339513" href="/book/show/330945.Genghis">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019174-terence?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311688200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15922993292235335061">A weak-kneed three stars for this one, and that’s primarily because Mongol history holds a particular fascination for me. If this were a novel about the early years of the Sun King or the first Incan ruler, I’m not sure I’d continue.<br/><br/>The writing isn’t bad, and sometimes approaches a level that makes readers feel they’re there. Examples of this are an early scene where Temujin climbs a steep hillside to capture two eagle chicks for his father and the scene where he’s tortured by his father’s erstw</span>
  <span id="freeText15922993292235335061" style="display:none">A weak-kneed three stars for this one, and that’s primarily because Mongol history holds a particular fascination for me. If this were a novel about the early years of the Sun King or the first Incan ruler, I’m not sure I’d continue.<br /><br />The writing isn’t bad, and sometimes approaches a level that makes readers feel they’re there. Examples of this are an early scene where Temujin climbs a steep hillside to capture two eagle chicks for his father and the scene where he’s tortured by his father’s erstwhile bondsman, Eeluk, who has usurped control of the nomad band the future khan’s father had ruled. A failure is the set up of Temujin’s relationship with Borte, his wife. Rather it’s the lack of one. Iggulden introduces Borte as a 12-year-old tomboy who’s so dirty that Temujin is hard pressed to recognize whether she’s a boy or a girl, and his primary concern is that she’s not too ugly. Yet when she follows him one night and he stumbles upon her, the sound of her voice and a touch of her cheek and it’s love.<br /><br />Which points up another issue with the book, and that’s that, with the exception of Temujin, none of the other characters – Hoelun (his mother) or his brothers, Bekter, Khasar, Kachiun &amp; Temuge, for example – come alive as individuals.<br /><br />I will mention one of the better aspects of Iggulden’s writing – since I do want to provide another example of the author’s skills – and that is his depiction of the ethical outlook of nomad life. There’s only one instance where I think he stumbles in this regard (Temujin’s reaction to Borte’s abduction and rape*/!); otherwise, the reader does spend a lot of time in a truly alien way of life.<br /><br />I’ll continue with the series because the writing is engaging <i>enough</i> and because of the Mongol angle but unless the characters become more interesting or the writing becomes significantly better, I doubt these books will be well remembered a decade from now.<br /><br />* The abduction is historical though the perpetrators &amp; its length were changed.<br /><br />! My objection is to the sensitivity with which Temujin deals with her. I’m not saying he wouldn’t (and didn’t) act so “civilized,” but there was no building of a foundation to make it believable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15922993292235335061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2507586642" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2507586642" />
    <a title="Zoe Saadia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5852913-zoe-saadia"><img alt="Zoe Saadia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521925592p2/5852913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2507586642?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoe Saadia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoe Saadia" href="/user/show/5852913-zoe-saadia">Zoe Saadia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2507586642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9287613284984980310">Enjoyed this first book of the "Conqueror" series very much. For me it combined the best of historical fiction, with a seemingly thorough enough research and a plot-driven story full of action that didn't make it feel like an history lesson (I'm buried in history in my daily life, so when I pick a book that has nothing to do with my own fairly narrow field, I want to enjoy the story and learn without feeling that an history lesson or customs of unknown culture were forced on me - in other words,</span>
  <span id="freeText9287613284984980310" style="display:none">Enjoyed this first book of the "Conqueror" series very much. For me it combined the best of historical fiction, with a seemingly thorough enough research and a plot-driven story full of action that didn't make it feel like an history lesson (I'm buried in history in my daily life, so when I pick a book that has nothing to do with my own fairly narrow field, I want to enjoy the story and learn without feeling that an history lesson or customs of unknown culture were forced on me - in other words, historical fiction, in my opinion, should be entertaining and not only enriching).<br />Well, Temujin's story in this first book of the series answered this criteria of mine perfectly. It was difficult to put down and between one action-tension-filled-scene and another I found myself on the edge of my seat and sneaking more reading when I needed to do other things. They leapt from the pages so very alive for me, Temujin, his brothers, especially Kachiun and Khasar, his mother Hoelun and his father Yesugei, his future wife Borte. The whole scenery around them, their customs and way of life, were more than fascinating, recreated again with liveliness and no attempt to "europenize" those, not to my knowledge (which again is absolutely minimal when it comes to the Mongolian People, so I can't vouch for the authenticity, but to me the story felt authentic enough, presented in a natural way. I felt the same reading "Shogun" - one moment a completely outlandish custom, a few chapters later I can't see a more natural behavior and horrified when this or that character doesn't follow it or doesn't understand. To me it's the best of historical fiction, to be able to put reader into a foreign-to-him setting so naturally and smoothly.)<br />I already started on the book two. Hope it will be as good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9287613284984980310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
