    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/86380-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595021786p2/86380.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49627616?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/86380-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jo by: </span>
      Goodreads
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86380-jo?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49627616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2190804010145522070">This was one of those books that I found nearly impossible to put down once I started reading. Dealing with Genghis Kahn's early years, from just prior to the death of his father through him actually naming himself as Genghis, the plot sucks you in and makes you feel everything that he (and his family) go through as he experiences the events that turn him from a Mongol named Temujin to a man who literally changed the face of the world. The characters are <i>alive</i> on the pages, breathing and moving </span>
  <span id="freeText2190804010145522070" style="display:none">This was one of those books that I found nearly impossible to put down once I started reading. Dealing with Genghis Kahn's early years, from just prior to the death of his father through him actually naming himself as Genghis, the plot sucks you in and makes you feel everything that he (and his family) go through as he experiences the events that turn him from a Mongol named Temujin to a man who literally changed the face of the world. The characters are <i>alive</i> on the pages, breathing and moving and living, and the descriptions are lush and rich with images that linger long after you've turned the last page.<br /><br />It's described as historical fiction, and the author freely admits he changed some things (mostly names of certain people and some locations), but it feels far more factual than many biographies that I've read. I plan on picking up the second book in the series, <i>Genghis: Lords of the Bow</i>, and definitely recommend this one to everyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2190804010145522070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_332580360" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/332580360" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/332580360?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6568175-genghis">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer332580360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8326915666862730974">This book tracks the origins of Genghis Kahn (Chinggis Haan), from his birth as Temujin of the Mongol tribe calling itself The Wolves, to his claiming of the title of Kahn of the Sea of Grass in the late 12th century.<br/><br/>I found the book engaging from start to finish. Conn Iggulden does a good job of telling a tale set in a harsh landscape, home to a warrior culture that was proud and often cruel. Weakness is despised and men are expected to suppress outward displays of emotion and instead show the </span>
  <span id="freeText8326915666862730974" style="display:none">This book tracks the origins of Genghis Kahn (Chinggis Haan), from his birth as Temujin of the Mongol tribe calling itself The Wolves, to his claiming of the title of Kahn of the Sea of Grass in the late 12th century.<br /><br />I found the book engaging from start to finish. Conn Iggulden does a good job of telling a tale set in a harsh landscape, home to a warrior culture that was proud and often cruel. Weakness is despised and men are expected to suppress outward displays of emotion and instead show the “Cold Face,” especially in the face of their enemies.<br /><br /> This was a rather straight forward easy read as we get snap shots of the major events in Temujin's life, from his happy early years when his father, Yesugei, was khan of the Wolves, to his betrayal, to his vision of uniting all the Mongol tribes under one banner – his banner. Iggulden gives us a fair look at the male dominated culture of the Mongols and we learn a bit about their major enemies, the <i>Tartar</i>, as well as the <i>Chin</i> who try to play the two off against each other.<br /><br />There’s plenty of blood-letting. Plenty of battle action centred around archery, given that archery, particularly horse archery, was the Mongols' weapon of mass destruction. Temujin AKA Genghis starts out pretty early in life as an uber archer, and then adds uber swordsman to his repertoire and finally uber uber general. If this wasn't based somewhat in reality one could be forgiven for complaining that Temujin is way over-powered (and he probably is in this book at times) and the narrative moving quickly over a number of years did make it seem that success came too easily for him. Also, the fact that this reads like every boys fantasy of ninja/samarai badassery probably put a bit of a dampener on the gravitas that the historical Genghis arguably warrants. But I didn't really care about that. Cool is cool and this appealed to my inner ninja and there were a few scenes that had me reaching for my sword and showing my enemy the “Cold Face” - which I consider to be a fair achievement given that my enemy looked absolutely ridiculous staring back at me from the mirror wielding his plastic lightsaber.<br /><br />A quick, easy, enjoyable read and I’m off to start the next book in the series<br /><br /><br />4.25 ninja stars.<br /><br />PS: Yes yes, <i>I know</i> Ninja and Samurai have nothing to do with Mongols - but little boys don't.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8326915666862730974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2839655148?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken Hammond" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken Hammond" href="/user/show/74625627-ken-hammond">Ken Hammond</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2839655148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7158601617225627722">Genghis: Birth of an Empire (Conqueror, #1) <br/>by Conn Iggulden <br/><br/>This book which only deals with Temujin's early life up until he changes his name from Temujin to become forever known as Genghis Khan of all the Mongols, and conqueror of the largest continuous land empire anyone has ever seen before or since.<br/><br/>Having only recently read Frank McLynn history of Ghengis this was a more personal & freer styled view into the early years, it created some wide pictures in my mind, the wide open plain scenes m</span>
  <span id="freeText7158601617225627722" style="display:none">Genghis: Birth of an Empire (Conqueror, #1) <br />by Conn Iggulden <br /><br />This book which only deals with Temujin's early life up until he changes his name from Temujin to become forever known as Genghis Khan of all the Mongols, and conqueror of the largest continuous land empire anyone has ever seen before or since.<br /><br />Having only recently read Frank McLynn history of Ghengis this was a more personal &amp; freer styled view into the early years, it created some wide pictures in my mind, the wide open plain scenes made me feel like I was on those plains with a whole head of hair and the wind blowing in my face. Then there were the principal characters mind set their way of thinking as written by Conn seemed just what any person would do if in that situation, (only if you really truly believe shut those eyes and imagine your are a Mongol horse archer galloping headlong into your enemies come on you can do it). Having never read anything of Conn's works before this was rather easy to follow &amp; really enjoyable. I loved the determination and never say die attitude of Temujin like when captured and thrown in a pit to be sacrificed, but his self belief and sheer tenacity shone through plus some luck. Anyway I imagine the following books will portray more of Genghis rise to power.<br /><br />Isolated and banished by his fathers liege man Eeluk, after his fathers assassination in the hopes they will die in the wilderness. But Temujins mother Hoelun is shrewd, resourceful and they survive, but Temijun in frustration murders his older brother Bekter to his mothers anger. later Eeluk captures Temujin but he escapes with help from Arslan &amp; Jelme his fathers loyal warriors. After years of gaining more and more numbers from other wandering isolated families and becoming a master of tactics and guerrilla attacks against their mortal Tartan enemies he builds up a form of warfare knowledge that will eventually become unbeatable and superior to anything around them at that time.<br /><br />Will have to mark to read the next in the series to soon as able.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7158601617225627722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1566810197" />

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1566810197?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott  Hitchcock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott  Hitchcock" href="/user/show/50894754-scott-hitchcock">Scott  Hitchcock</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6568175-genghis">review of another edition</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50894754-scott-hitchcock?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50894754-scott-hitchcock?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1566810197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6294243758420869234">It would be very easy for an author to take an iconic character such as this and try to go for something almost more mythical. It would be equally as tempting to make the story one of just blood and war. Those would make for good and entertaining stories. What makes for a great story is contrast. Contrast makes the savagery and epic events that much better. <br/><br/>The author shapes him and his brothers and gives us their hopes, dreams and fears that any children would have. The events change him, give </span>
  <span id="freeText6294243758420869234" style="display:none">It would be very easy for an author to take an iconic character such as this and try to go for something almost more mythical. It would be equally as tempting to make the story one of just blood and war. Those would make for good and entertaining stories. What makes for a great story is contrast. Contrast makes the savagery and epic events that much better. <br /><br />The author shapes him and his brothers and gives us their hopes, dreams and fears that any children would have. The events change him, give him direction and purpose through their brutal trials. The empathetic qualities given to the characters gives the contrast to the brutal lives they lived enduring an arid environment where winters can reach -20F. <br /><br />Simply a great historical fiction piece. I look forward to the other four books in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6294243758420869234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128972483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9644426502570293625">Update-<br/><br/>I passed this book to one of my employees. He does NOT read for enjoyment. I promised him he would love this book so he said he would give it a try. Yesterday, I saw him with book 2 and asked him what was up. His explanation- "I read book 1 every night for the past week and all weekend long". THAT is how good the book is, it made a non-reader into a reader and was so good, he bought book 2!<br/><br/>My review below:<br/><br/>Wow, wow, did I mention wow? This book was a history lesson, an action movie, and a </span>
  <span id="freeText9644426502570293625" style="display:none">Update-<br /><br />I passed this book to one of my employees. He does NOT read for enjoyment. I promised him he would love this book so he said he would give it a try. Yesterday, I saw him with book 2 and asked him what was up. His explanation- "I read book 1 every night for the past week and all weekend long". THAT is how good the book is, it made a non-reader into a reader and was so good, he bought book 2!<br /><br />My review below:<br /><br />Wow, wow, did I mention wow? This book was a history lesson, an action movie, and a tale of family loyalty all tied into one. I would have never read this book if it didn't come with a high recommendation from a friend. Her recommendations have all turned out to be terrific reads so I trusted her when she recommended this book.<br /><br />It took me about 100 pages to get into the story. It seemed like a boy's adventure book in the beginning. However, once I was past the initial 100 pages, it was hard to put the book down. Literally, I was walking around my house, holding the book (a hard cover so this was a difficult task) trying to finish just one more page.<br /><br />I can't wait to read book 2. I'm going to give my heart a while to calm itself. The battle scenes are intense but well worth the read!<br /><br />Did I mention wow?<br /><br />Update- added it to my favorite book list.</span>

<div id="review_1525997129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1525997129" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1525997129?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=chinese-translation">chinese-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=great">great</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=wish-i-could-write-like-this">wish-i-could-write-like-this</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1525997129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5904678223044733700">The first volume of Conn Iggulden's historical novel series: <i>Conqueror</i> series tells an remarkable and formidable tale of Genghis Khan's origin and the birth of the Mongol Empire.<br/><br/>Note: for some unknown reason the Chinese translation duds the book's title as <i>Conqueror: Wolf of the Plain/征服者︰瀚海蒼狼</i> instead of <i>Genghis: Birth of an Empire</i>. <br/><br/>As the second son of Yesügei (leader of the Borjigin clan), the young Temüjin lived a comfortable life, but his father was later assassinated and the clan chose a ne</span>
  <span id="freeText5904678223044733700" style="display:none">The first volume of Conn Iggulden's historical novel series: <i>Conqueror</i> series tells an remarkable and formidable tale of Genghis Khan's origin and the birth of the Mongol Empire.<br /><br />Note: for some unknown reason the Chinese translation duds the book's title as <i>Conqueror: Wolf of the Plain/征服者︰瀚海蒼狼</i> instead of <i>Genghis: Birth of an Empire</i>. <br /><br />As the second son of Yesügei (leader of the Borjigin clan), the young Temüjin lived a comfortable life, but his father was later assassinated and the clan chose a new leader then Temüjin and his family was abandoned on the harsh plain for death. Being forced to survive with only the clothes on their backs and their wits, the family went up against impossible odds and committed the unthinkable for survival. Aside from the despair need to survive, the burning desire for revenge was the driving force that kept the young Temüjin and his brothers going. <br /><br />This book is not only just an intriguing coming-of-age, survival-themed and 'rags to rich' story, it also gives us a vivid picture of how life on the Mongolian harsh plain was like at that time. I also like how the different tribes' way of life is described with rich details. (the author is known for going to Mongolia for research)<br /><br />Also I admire how the author also expresses the spirit and morals of the Mongol people of that time: they lived at the mercy of the harsh plain; outside of their horses, livestock, weapons and their own wits these people had nothing to depend on. Kill or be killed, rob or be robbed, winner takes all, was more or less their way of life. And how the author writes about those details is simply..........impressive. Through his writing and the development of Temüjin who grows from a boy who lost everything, to the leader of a small band of bandits, then eventually a young Khan who sets his sight on conquering the entire plain.<br /><br />There are many shocking twists in Temüjin's tale, for example <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he killed his older brother after the latter kept food for himself when the rest of the family was starving <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and I think you will enjoy them as well.<br /><br />Last but not least, the final battle at the ending part of the book is also extraordinarily written, the author writes like he is bringing you right to the battle field and letting you experience the wind blowing past you as the riders matched down the hill, as arrows flying through the sky and battle cries were shout across the plain. <br /><br />PS: please notice that this book is a historical novel, so many details aren't exactly accurate. <br /><br />My review for the sequel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1526013400">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5904678223044733700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_47422367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47422367" />
    <a title="Sandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/811687-sandi"><img alt="Sandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404709147p2/811687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47422367?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandi" href="/user/show/811687-sandi">Sandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone, especially teenage boys</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sandi by: </span>
      Won through First Reads
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/811687-sandi?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/811687-sandi?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/811687-sandi?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47422367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4956372112680651427">I started <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1283235.Genghis_Birth_of_an_Empire__Conqueror_book_1_' title='Genghis Birth of an Empire (Conqueror book 1) by Conn Iggulden' rel='nofollow noopener'>Genghis Birth of an Empire</a> with a bit of trepidation. It starts out like a book for teenage boys. Indeed, it is a book that should have a great deal of appeal to teenage boys. Shortly after I did my eyeroll over brotherly rivalry and impending manhood, I really got sucked into the story. In many ways, this book reminded me more of epic fantasy than historical fiction. A young prince finds himself in the lowest of situations, facing death. He finds a way to survive and rises to his inte</span>
  <span id="freeText4956372112680651427" style="display:none">I started <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1283235.Genghis_Birth_of_an_Empire__Conqueror_book_1_" title="Genghis Birth of an Empire (Conqueror book 1) by Conn Iggulden" rel="nofollow noopener">Genghis Birth of an Empire</a> with a bit of trepidation. It starts out like a book for teenage boys. Indeed, it is a book that should have a great deal of appeal to teenage boys. Shortly after I did my eyeroll over brotherly rivalry and impending manhood, I really got sucked into the story. In many ways, this book reminded me more of epic fantasy than historical fiction. A young prince finds himself in the lowest of situations, facing death. He finds a way to survive and rises to his intended greatness. The Mongolian setting is not unlike a setting in a fantasy novel. I usually think of historical fiction as being more romantic and less epic.<br /><br />I knew very little about Genghis Khan when I started this novel. For one, I had no idea that his life and conquests were so heavily documented. In his afterward, Iggulden says that he relies heavily on primary sources for the history in this novel. He manages to take that documentation and create characters that truly come alive. His portrayal of Temujin's mother was excellent. A very minor gripe for me was that Iggulden never tells us when the story is taking place. Looking online, I found that Ghengis Khan lived from 1162 to 1227 A.D. I had no idea that his reign was so recent and I wish Iggulden had included that information in his otherwise excellent afterword. <br /><br />Now, I'm not going to pretend that this is great literature or even a good history. It's neither. However, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1283235.Genghis_Birth_of_an_Empire__Conqueror_book_1_" title="Genghis Birth of an Empire (Conqueror book 1) by Conn Iggulden" rel="nofollow noopener">Genghis Birth of an Empire</a> is a wonderfully entertaining read that also managed to teach me about a piece of history I knew nothing about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4956372112680651427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2305203986" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305203986" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63168028-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516912354p2/63168028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305203986?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/63168028-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305203986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer784074704620098944"><b> Visionary </b><br/>One of the greatest empires ever built, if not the greatest. <br/><br/>Yesugei, the khan of the Wolf tribe, his wife, Hoelun, his sons Temujin, Bekter, Khasar, Kachiun and Temuge, and his daughter Borte, live a warring and perfidious existence against other tribes on the Mongolian steppes. Yesugei dies after an attack and leaves the leadership open to Eeluk (his bondsman) with his sons not being old enough to take control. Eeluk exiles Hoelun and her children to live an abandoned harsh life wit</span>
  <span id="freeText784074704620098944" style="display:none"><b> Visionary </b><br />One of the greatest empires ever built, if not the greatest. <br /><br />Yesugei, the khan of the Wolf tribe, his wife, Hoelun, his sons Temujin, Bekter, Khasar, Kachiun and Temuge, and his daughter Borte, live a warring and perfidious existence against other tribes on the Mongolian steppes. Yesugei dies after an attack and leaves the leadership open to Eeluk (his bondsman) with his sons not being old enough to take control. Eeluk exiles Hoelun and her children to live an abandoned harsh life with no dwelling, no food, no animals, no horses and no weapons. Surely as winter descends it is only a matter of time before they all perish. <br /><br />And so the story of one of the greatest rises to power begins. The story of Temujin for all eras is totally inspiring. How he used strategy, tactics, politics, force and cunning to unite the tribes. His greatest battle to this point against the Tartars, see his father’s clan the Wolves come to participate. After the victory, Temujin and Eeluk fight to resolve old vendettas, leaving Temujin victorious and leader of many of the tribes on the plains.<br /><br />The book is a wonderful example of historical fiction where we get to know so much about the times of the foundation and growth of the Mongol empire and the birth of Genghis Khan. The narrative creates a personal insight into the characters that are inspirational, loyal and hard as nails, and a storyline that is breath-taking. The harshness of the environment and how they survived is exceptionally well told.</span>
  <a data-text-id="784074704620098944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6923059201515707192">Rating 5* out of 5. This book is a stunning achievement. It's loosely based on fact and describes the early life of Temujin, the man who became known as Djengis Khan. It's one of the best books in the category historical fiction, that I've ever come across.<br/><br/>Temujin is only 11 years old when his father dies and the clan disowns them. The widow and her children are expected to die the first winter, but somehow they survive. Temujin is a young man of vision and tenacity, which is required when the c</span>
  <span id="freeText6923059201515707192" style="display:none">Rating 5* out of 5. This book is a stunning achievement. It's loosely based on fact and describes the early life of Temujin, the man who became known as Djengis Khan. It's one of the best books in the category historical fiction, that I've ever come across.<br /><br />Temujin is only 11 years old when his father dies and the clan disowns them. The widow and her children are expected to die the first winter, but somehow they survive. Temujin is a young man of vision and tenacity, which is required when the clan comes back to check whether the strays have died or not. It's not exactly a coming of age tale in the usual sense, but it is certainly a satisfying story of survival and revenge.<br /><br />Brilliant book, vibrant characters and the windswept plains of Mongolia - highly recommended!<br /><br />I'm moving on to the next book in the series, and this time on paper and not as unabridged audio as this first one. It took much longer than I would have liked!<br /><br /></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=mongolia">mongolia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=hf">hf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39999273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5354560888592079294">This is an action filled tale about Genghis Kahn. It is cinematic in tone, and by that I mean it is plot oriented, with one exciting thing after another happening in rapid succession. I could accept the violence when I felt it was motivated by the need to either kill or be killed; I could accept it when he was younger and simply fighting to survive. By the end, it was simply too much. Lots of gory fighting, with some love thrown in too. <br/><br/>What did I learn about the Mongolian way of life? Very litt</span>
  <span id="freeText5354560888592079294" style="display:none">This is an action filled tale about Genghis Kahn. It is cinematic in tone, and by that I mean it is plot oriented, with one exciting thing after another happening in rapid succession. I could accept the violence when I felt it was motivated by the need to either kill or be killed; I could accept it when he was younger and simply fighting to survive. By the end, it was simply too much. Lots of gory fighting, with some love thrown in too. <br /><br />What did I learn about the Mongolian way of life? Very little, that I didn’t know before. Sky burials are much better depicted in “Sky Burial: An Epic Love Story of Tibet” by Xinran, which is a biography. <br /><br />There is a detailed Afterword that explains what if fact and what is fiction, and the author does stick to the known fact for much of the tale. <br /><br />It is just not my kind of book, but sure, others may like it.<br /><br />ETA: I will be reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/93426.Genghis_Khan_and_the_Making_of_the_Modern_World" title="Genghis Khan and the Making of the Modern World by Jack Weatherford" rel="nofollow noopener">Genghis Khan and the Making of the Modern World</a> as a counterbalance to what I have gotten from Iggulden's book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5354560888592079294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13367674899451769491" style="display:none">Sorry it has taken me so long to do this review, but I had computer difficulties, and haven't been able to get on the internet since March. Fortunately, all is better now.<br />I won this book earlier this year. It was awesome, I truly could not put it down. It was a incredible page-turner for me. I really want to get the rest of the series. I have got to find out what happens next!<br />I read this book in 2 days, and it was very enlightening about the life of Genghis Khan. I never really knew much about him, but found the book really inspiring because in the face of insurmountable odds, and unbelievable obstacles, Genghis thrived. He seemed to draw strength from what would have crushed most. After reading this, I was talking non-stop about this book to everyone... I really enjoyed it.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MFk/Qzv7eqrLIw7ifPJidB8i8N+rsMzNdfOGEe8x8kS95494YXyFWj3PPl4JxbkKj0o/tx8yoOjSUnxOMyA3zA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_3276012'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3276012-agincourt?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Agincourt<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/12542.Bernard_Cornwell?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Bernard Cornwell<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.12 avg rating &mdash; 24,125 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2008\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer11430377433959017051\">Agincourt is one of the epic battles of history. It was fought by two badly matched armies that met in atrocious conditions on St Crispin\'s Day 1415, and resulted in an extraordinary victory that was celebrated in England long before Shakespeare immo<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11430377433959017051\" style=\"display:none\">Agincourt is one of the epic battles of history. It was fought by two badly matched armies that met in atrocious conditions on St Crispin\'s Day 1415, and resulted in an extraordinary victory that was celebrated in England long before Shakespeare immortalised it in Henry V. It has always been held to be the triumph of the longbow against the armoured knight, and of the common man against the feudal aristocrat, but those are history\'s myths. Bernard Cornwell, who has long wanted to write this story, depicts the reality behind the myths.\n\nNicholas Hook is an English archer. He seems born to trouble and, when his lord orders him to London as part of a force sent to quell an expected Lollard uprising, Nick\'s headstrong behaviour leads to him being proscribed an outlaw. He finds refuge across the Channel, part of an English mercenary force protecting the town of Soissons against the French. What happened at the Siege of Soissons shocked all Europe, and propels Nick back to England where he is enrolled in the archer companyof the doughty Sir John Cornwaille, a leader of Henry V\'s army. The army was superb, but sickness and the unexpected French defiance at Harfleur, reduce it to near-shambolic condition. Henry stubbornly refuses to accept defeat and, in appalling weather, leads his shrunken force to what appears to be inevitable disaster.\n\nAzincourt culminates in the battle. Seen from several points of view on the English side, but also from the French ranks, the scene is vivid, convincing and compelling. Bernard Cornwell has a great understanding of men at war and battlefields and this is his masterpiece. This is what it must have been like to fight at Agincourt.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11430377433959017051\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/119121.Conn_Iggulden">About Conn Iggulden</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/119121.Conn_Iggulden"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1235073163p3/119121.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1076899907689023169"><i>Also publishes under author name <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16155974.C_F__Iggulden' title='C.F. Iggulden' rel='nofollow noopener'>C.F. Iggulden</a>.</i><br/><br/>I was born in the normal way in 1971, and vaguely remember half-pennies and sixpences. I have written for as long as I can remember: poetry, short stories and novels. It’s what I always wanted to do and read English at London University with writing in mind. I taught English for seven years and was Head of English at St. Gregory’s RC High School in Lo</span>
  <span id="freeText1076899907689023169" style="display:none"><i>Also publishes under author name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16155974.C_F__Iggulden" title="C.F. Iggulden" rel="nofollow noopener">C.F. Iggulden</a>.</i><br /><br />I was born in the normal way in 1971, and vaguely remember half-pennies and sixpences. I have written for as long as I can remember: poetry, short stories and novels. It’s what I always wanted to do and read English at London University with writing in mind. I taught English for seven years and was Head of English at St. Gregory’s RC High School in London by the end of that period. I have enormous respect for those who still labour at the chalk-face. In truth, I can’t find it in me to miss the grind of paperwork and initiatives. I do miss the camaraderie of the smokers’ room, as well as the lessons where their faces lit up as they understood what I was wittering on about.<br /><br />My mother is Irish and from an early age she told me history as an exciting series of stories – with dates. My great-grandfather was a Seannachie, so I suppose story-telling is in the genes somewhere. My father flew in Bomber Command in WWII, then taught maths and science. Perhaps crucially, he also loved poetry and cracking good tales. Though it seems a dated idea now, I began teaching when boys were told only girls were good at English, despite the great names that must spring to mind after that statement. My father loved working with wood and equations, but he also recited ‘Vitai Lampada’ with a gleam in his eye and that matters, frankly.<br /><br />I’ve always loved historical fiction as a genre and cut my teeth on Hornblower and Tai-Pan, Flashman, Sharpe and Jack Aubrey. I still remember the sheer joy of reading my first Patrick O’Brian book and discovering there were nineteen more in the series. I love just about anything by David Gemmell, or Peter F. Hamilton or Wilbur Smith. I suppose the one thing that links all those is the love of a good tale.<br /><br />That’s about it for the moment. If you’d like to get in touch with me leave a comment in the forum or you can tweet me @Conn_Iggulden. I’ll leave it there for the moment. If you’ve read my books, you know an awful lot about the way I think already. There’s no point overdoing it.<br /><br />Conn Iggulden<br /></span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_12280500').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_12280500').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_12280500').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
